  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_61112792-9cee-4b5a-bfaa-39dee600f3c2'
      });

<div id="review_72931367" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/72931367" />
    <a title="Meghan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2788534-meghan"><img alt="Meghan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514351832p2/2788534.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/72931367?book_show_action=true">Sep 29, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Meghan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Meghan" href="/user/show/2788534-meghan">Meghan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Cat lovers</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Meghan by: </span>
      My friend Allison recommended the series to me
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer72931367&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer72931367" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13419447139301389937">This book starts out in conflict; the Clans are on the verge of fighting one another because the lake where the Clans make their home has been mysteriously drained of almost all its water. RiverClan starts causing problems by claiming the land where the lake used to be, and through all this the Clans grow thirstier and thirstier. <br/><br/>Meanwhile in ThunderClan, cats are growing up. Poppyfrost is due to have kits, and six-moon old kits are being made apprentices, mainly Dovekit and Ivykit. Dovekit beco</span>
  <span id="freeText13419447139301389937" style="display:none">This book starts out in conflict; the Clans are on the verge of fighting one another because the lake where the Clans make their home has been mysteriously drained of almost all its water. RiverClan starts causing problems by claiming the land where the lake used to be, and through all this the Clans grow thirstier and thirstier. <br /><br />Meanwhile in ThunderClan, cats are growing up. Poppyfrost is due to have kits, and six-moon old kits are being made apprentices, mainly Dovekit and Ivykit. Dovekit becomes Lionblaze's apprentice and Ivypaw becomes Cinderheart's. Life goes on for a while, then Dovepaw starts discovering her gift of sensing animals and events that are far away from her, and she finds out that something is damming the stream, causing the drainage of the lake. <br /><br />The Clans each send a patrol to find out who (or what) blocked up the lake and the cats must stop the threat from destroying the Clans.<br /><br />This book was well-written and kept me on edge while I was reading it. This series gets better and better and I can't wait to find out what happens to the chosen Three. It's a shame that the next one (Fading Echoes) doesn't come out until next April, but that'll come soon enough. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13419447139301389937" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer7890805831617754265">I am a big fan of Erin Hunter and, more specifically, the Warriors saga. I fell in love with the cats and the books themselves a few years ago, and avidly read them until I reached this point. Though I still read, I couldn't help but ask myself over and over "WHEN IS THIS GOING TO END?"<br/> <br/>The storyline of the Power of Three just seems to carry along in Omen of the Stars, and you start to wonder if the Erins were just trying to fit random things in to take up space and make a new series.<br/><br/>The first t</span>
  <span id="freeText7890805831617754265" style="display:none">I am a big fan of Erin Hunter and, more specifically, the Warriors saga. I fell in love with the cats and the books themselves a few years ago, and avidly read them until I reached this point. Though I still read, I couldn't help but ask myself over and over "WHEN IS THIS GOING TO END?"<br /> <br />The storyline of the Power of Three just seems to carry along in Omen of the Stars, and you start to wonder if the Erins were just trying to fit random things in to take up space and make a new series.<br /><br />The first two series, the original Warriors and The New Prophecy, were both spellbinding and kept you entertained and wondering what would happen next over and over. They include all of the literary elements a good series/book should have, but you reach the Power of Three and it all starts to fade. <br /><br />Sorry, Erins.<br /><br />The Overachiever.xx</span>

<div id="review_159052614" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/159052614" />
    <a title="Emily" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4460586-emily"><img alt="Emily" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/159052614?book_show_action=true">Apr 05, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily" href="/user/show/4460586-emily">Emily</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer159052614" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9679626153361722577">I am such a dork, lol BUT I LOVE THESE BOOKS!!!! I read them over the past two years probably and I always found them to be great!!!! Cats that talk...ya I know sounds stupid but I love cats well actually animals in general so these books are great for me! Erin Hunter does a great job spinning tales of the lives of the 4 clans of cats. I couldn't pick a favorite in the series and be set on it, but if I had to it would be the first one Into The Wild, because in my eyes that is what started the wh</span>
  <span id="freeText9679626153361722577" style="display:none">I am such a dork, lol BUT I LOVE THESE BOOKS!!!! I read them over the past two years probably and I always found them to be great!!!! Cats that talk...ya I know sounds stupid but I love cats well actually animals in general so these books are great for me! Erin Hunter does a great job spinning tales of the lives of the 4 clans of cats. I couldn't pick a favorite in the series and be set on it, but if I had to it would be the first one Into The Wild, because in my eyes that is what started the whole series and is therefore connected to all of them!!! Before this book Jayfeather and LIonblaze two of the three cats destined to hold the power of the stars in their paws lost their dear sister Hollyleaf. They thought she was part of the prophecy but she ended up dying in a terrible accident in tunnels underground. Still mourning over Hollyleaf's death Jayfeather and Lionblaze look for hope in Whitewings new kits. Ivypaw and Dovepaw. Is there hope for the prophecy?? Well this book will tell all!!! Which one of the new kits will hold the power of the stars in their paws...read this amazing Erin Hunter book to find out!!!!<br /><br />At the same time that Lionblaze and Jayfeather have to worry about the prophecy they are also in danger from their families deadly past. In the last book the truth about the brothers parents came out... Squirrelflight and Brambleclaw were the parents of Lionblaze, Jayfeather, and Hollyleaf. Or at least that is what everyone thought until the truth came out...and EVERYONE learned that their real parents were Leafpool (Squirrelflight's sister) and Crowfeather. The bad part to that parentage is that Leafpool was from Thunderclan and Crowfeather was Windclan, that is a against the warrior code for cat clans to have mates in other clans. They broke rules to be together and what is even worse is that Leafpool was a medicine cat and they aren't allowed to have mates and or kits. So it was a scandal in the clans, and they lied about it. Lionblaze and Jayfeather are half clan cats and now everyone knows, and there is nothing they can do about it. Anger over this affair/scandal runs deep in some cats hearts. Revenge is taken and from this book lays a path of destruction to the next in the series, Fading Echoes. <br />On top of all those problems surrounding just Lionblaze and his brother Jayfeather, is the survival of all the clans. A much bigger problem that involves every cat from every clan is going down!!!! There is a drought and it is summer time. Already extremely hot, no rain and whats worse the water flowing through the main stream stops. No cat knows what is wrong(well maybe one does!) and all the clans are doomed unless someone can bring the water back. Figure out the fate of the clans and more specifically Lionblaze, Jayfeather, and the mystery kitten with the power of the stars in her paws by reading this amazing book, The Fourth Apprentice!!!!!!!! <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9679626153361722577" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText13252230896768712762" style="display:none"> Have you ever had a time when it was horrible just the way it was but you have a someone that was unwell that added fuel to the fire. Leopardstar is suffering and no medicine cat could prevent it form taking her lives, everything was only known to river clan till Dovewing the third cat in the prophecy due to the tragic end of the prophecy but every ending is a beginning. At the gathering she calmed that the lake belongs to river clan and that wind clan ,shadow clan and thunder clan were stealing there fish but she overlooked the fact that there was a drought going on.Firestar was on a patrol when a fox ambushed his patrol but he manged to drive it off but it caused him to loose another life just like what Lepardstar is going through. <br /><br /> Dovewing has the power of stars in her paw just like Jaypaw and Lionblaze so it is not a shocker that she had a dream of a brown animal blocking the stream that provides water to the lake and at the gathering Firestar persuades all the clan leaders to join in but getting passed Lepardstar was not easy as he claimed that he wanted to invade river clan camp which was located all the way on the other side of the lake, but with the help of her trusted deputy Mistyfoot Firestar managed to get all the clans acceptation and in no time a patrol was organized to return the life back to the clans. The patrol encountered trouble but it was nothing compared to what to face in-other to be saviors, even thought they encountered trouble they found help too. Armed with this knowledge the clan cats head of to free the water but it was harder than they thought as the planned attack backfired and it turned to a fighting to survive, the brown animal slashed and bite at the clan cats, they we loosing the fight as one cat died and more being slashed at but they never gave up fighting even if all of them were covered in blood and wounds. Will the clan cats die trying or make up another plan? <br /><br /><br /> This book is great for people who like solving problems as there are more problems in this books as there are stars in the sky. The book was so well written that I sometimes forget that that I am reading and not there and it is so additive that you can't even stop reading no mater what.T his book is actually really different form all the other books yet it has some elements of classic warriors. I truly think that Mistyfoot will be a great leader but a dark time draws near.. </span>

  <span id="freeText15214613315965200342" style="display:none">Note: This review is for all of the Omen of the Stars books (see list at end of the review)<br /><br />The last two books of the Power of Three series were a bit disappointing, but the Omen of the Stars books definitely made up for it.<br /><br />Everything about these books is just so epic. It's the final showdown, between good and evil, the Dark Forest and StarClan. And the Clans are forced to pick a side. If you've read the Power of Three books, you know about the Prophecy (<i> There will be three, kin of Firestar's kin, who hold the power of the stars in their paws </i>) and it's finally fulfilled. <br /><br />Lots of action and in the last book, StarClan fights in the battle so it was good to see familiar faces from old books.<br /><br />My only complaint is that the actual battle doesn't happen until the last book. And there are six books in the Omen of the Stars series! So there's a lot of buildup, and some action that doesn't have to do with the battle. But the final battle is so amazing that it's worth it.<br /><br />Overall a very entertaining series, and the last book was so freaking worth it.<br /><br />Because there are so MANY books in the Warriors saga, here is the list (in order) of all the books in the main arc. <span id="freeTextContainer14549730672734996476">Jayfeather and Lionblaze still don't know who the third cat is supposed to be. It's either Ivypaw or Dovepaw...you don't know which until a few chapters into it.<br/>Meanwhile, the lake has dried up, RiverClan is accusing the other Clans of stealing prey, and the third cat (who will remain nameless) knows that something is upstream, blocking the water flow.<br/>All four Clans send cats on a mission to find the water and save the Clans (this whole "saving the Clans" thing happens a lot) but time is running</span>
  <span id="freeText14549730672734996476" style="display:none">Jayfeather and Lionblaze still don't know who the third cat is supposed to be. It's either Ivypaw or Dovepaw...you don't know which until a few chapters into it.<br />Meanwhile, the lake has dried up, RiverClan is accusing the other Clans of stealing prey, and the third cat (who will remain nameless) knows that something is upstream, blocking the water flow.<br />All four Clans send cats on a mission to find the water and save the Clans (this whole "saving the Clans" thing happens a lot) but time is running out and the fate of the Clans is resting on the shoulders of five warriors who become four, and an apprentice who knows more than she's telling....<br /><br />It's an ongoing adventure story that keeps going, in five different series so far. Honestly, what's not to like?<br /><br />This will only make sense if you've read the first three series of Warriors books. Just in case, I'll tell you what they are. Warriors, Warriors: The New Prophecy, Warriors: Power of Three, and Warriors: Omen of the Stars. If you like animals and fun explanations for things, and whole civilizations right under people's noses, you'll like this.</span>

<div id="review_1636039185" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1636039185" />
    <a title="Jaedan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48101518-jaedan"><img alt="Jaedan" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1636039185?book_show_action=true">May 12, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jaedan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jaedan" href="/user/show/48101518-jaedan">Jaedan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1636039185" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer789129325471376693">This was a great book. It was an interesting, exiting, and page turning book. It doesn't really make sense to tell the story line of the book in this review because no one would know what was going on or what I'm talking about it unless they read these books, but I'll do it anyways. The book start out with the two characters from the previous series, Jayfeather and Lionblaze, and a new character. Between the previous book and this one Dovekit and Ivykit were born. Jayfeather and Lionblaze had th</span>
  <span id="freeText789129325471376693" style="display:none">This was a great book. It was an interesting, exiting, and page turning book. It doesn't really make sense to tell the story line of the book in this review because no one would know what was going on or what I'm talking about it unless they read these books, but I'll do it anyways. The book start out with the two characters from the previous series, Jayfeather and Lionblaze, and a new character. Between the previous book and this one Dovekit and Ivykit were born. Jayfeather and Lionblaze had thought that Hollyleaf was the third one in the prophecy, but when she died, they knew it couldn't have been her. Dovekit and her sister Ivykit were both related to Firestar, so one of them could possibly be the third cat from the prophecy. While trying to find out which of them is the third cat, the lake is shrinking and shrinking. Every cat is starting to starve because of the effects of the lack of water, but one cat can do something that none other can, and knows what is causing the lake to shrink. Is it Dovekit, or Ivykit? Read to find out.</span>
  <a data-text-id="789129325471376693" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5044729199960717335">New story, new cycle for Warrior Cats. If there is one series I have loved there's definitely this one: the Warrior Cats. But as much as I do find the new characters quite nice, the new story still just as well-fitting to the last cycle, and the cats still just as cute (I need a break from cuteness), I really think the series need to finally and definitely stop (and I really mean it). I mean, the global story, as good as it is, is just getting too boring and repetitive. And even the first book o</span>
  <span id="freeText5044729199960717335" style="display:none">New story, new cycle for Warrior Cats. If there is one series I have loved there's definitely this one: the Warrior Cats. But as much as I do find the new characters quite nice, the new story still just as well-fitting to the last cycle, and the cats still just as cute (I need a break from cuteness), I really think the series need to finally and definitely stop (and I really mean it). I mean, the global story, as good as it is, is just getting too boring and repetitive. And even the first book of the fourth cycle(sigh...) has a plot that was just re-used and remixed from the third cycle. I think the author is DEFINITELY running out of ideas now. To be fair, I read the book in two days and seriously wasn't impressed by this start of the cycle. It is simply not creative enough compared to the other cycles. So I think, as good as is Warrior Cats, it is getting too much, and it needs to stop (actually it technically could have stopped before but whatever). Don't put hate comments after reading this please, I am a fan of Warrior Cats, don't get me wrong.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8350383245571717157">I'd probably give this book 3.5 stars. It seems to be a trend that the first book in a Warriors arc takes a while to get going- in this case, introducing some new characters and a problem that needed solving. The action towards the end regarding the beavers felt a bit rushed, too, but I did enjoy Jayfeather's chapters, as he discovered the growing conflict between starclan and the dark forest. This book might have taken too long for me to get into, but nonetheless it's onto the next one!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer3053918439&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3053918439" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16550291150033767574">Premise: In the six months since their secret was revealed and their sister was lost, Firestar's grandsons have struggled to move on. Now that they know Hollyleaf is not one of the three cats in the prophecy, the only thing Lionblaze and Jayfeather can do is wait to learn the identity of the third. Meanwhile, a scorching drought is drying up the lake – and heating up tensions between the four Clans. In the midst of all this uneasiness, the two brothers set their sights on one particularly gifted</span>
  <span id="freeText16550291150033767574" style="display:none">Premise: In the six months since their secret was revealed and their sister was lost, Firestar's grandsons have struggled to move on. Now that they know Hollyleaf is not one of the three cats in the prophecy, the only thing Lionblaze and Jayfeather can do is wait to learn the identity of the third. Meanwhile, a scorching drought is drying up the lake – and heating up tensions between the four Clans. In the midst of all this uneasiness, the two brothers set their sights on one particularly gifted apprentice. Could she be the one they've been waiting for?<br /><br />Story/Writing: At LAST! I FINALLY get to start reading the arc I have been waiting to read for the last three MONTHS ever since I first got back into the series! But if anything good came out of that time of waiting, it was the proper buildup of anticipation from reading all the books (chronologically) before this! Given the knowledge I have of the "Omen of the Stars" arc (little though it may be), I'm gonna go out on a limb and compare it to Phase Three of the MCU, which started with "Captain America: Civil War" and ended with "Avengers: Endgame." In this case, we start with "The Fourth Apprentice." I liked that there was a nod to the title of the arc in the prologue, given that that's how the third cat in the prophecy is revealed. To be fair, I think we knew it was gonna be Dovepaw anyway since hers is one of the three points of view we read through. Regardless, I thought this was a fantastic start to this game-changing arc! It begins six months after the "Power of Three" arc ended. I can only imagine how rocked the expectations of fans were at that point, not only by Hollyleaf's disappearance but also the revelation that she's not the third cat in the prophecy. It makes sense though given how earth-shattering the end of "Sunrise" was, at least for the Clans. Anyway, the book does such a good job transitioning readers from that arc into this new one. You really get the feel that time has passed and things are slowly starting to change, both in the living world of the Clans and in the spirit worlds of Star Clan and the Dark Forest. By the end of this particular book, there's this eerie sense of foreboding that a gigantically climactic battle is coming and it's gonna change everything, similar to how the MCU built up Thanos and his quest for the Infinity Stones. The Clans have now existed for (according to my estimates) fifty years, which is like centuries for a cat. That's a long and sordid history of lies, deceit, and all sorts of other evil deeds for the Dark Forest to feed on. With that in mind, we finally see why the prophecy was given to Firestar in the first place. The three gifted cats (Jayfeather, Lionblaze, and Dovepaw) are going to lead the Clans into battle against the Dark Forest and defeat them once and for all. And I for one cannot wait to see that happen!<br /><br />Characters: Speaking of that sense of things changing, I can only imagine what it was like for fans to read this when it first came out. I've been reading the series in chronological order, starting with the "Dawn of the Clans" arc. But that arc wasn't published until after this one wrapped up. I didn't start the series with Rusty and Graypaw and the Clans when they were first introduced. And yet, seeing these cats as old as they now are, with some even being on the brink of death, gave me this really surreal feeling. There's this sense of this passing of the torch to the new generation of which Jayfeather, Lionblaze, and Dovepaw are a part of. That said, getting to know that new generation has been a blast for me!<br /><br />Dovepaw – I can understand if fans were a bit worried with how Dovepaw's debut would turn out, wondering if she would turn out to be a Mary Sue kind of character. But for one thing, I do not like that term. Not only is it vague, it's almost exclusively applied to female characters. Furthermore, given how many titles I've read in this series and how well each of the characters in those titles were developed, I had few qualms going into this. And I'm happy to say that the Erin Hunter team quickly endeared me to Dovepaw! To continue the earlier analogy, she reminded me of Spider-Man when he made his debut in the MCU. She's a new young apprentice, eager to please her mentor, serve her Clan, and be in on the action. She's sweet and kind but also bright and clever. She's bold and eager to prove herself, yet she's not a show-off or a know-it-all. I thought her close relationship with her sister Ivypaw was sweet. I thought it was perfect that Lionblaze was appointed as her mentor, not just because they're both part of the prophecy but also because they had a great big brother-little sister sort of chemistry. And based on what I read in this book alone, I think Tigerheart and Dovepaw would be cute together, even if they are from different Clans. I also thought her powers were pretty cool, like a sort of radar of the senses. In the hands of a less-talented author, this would open up a ton of plot holes. Fortunately, these authors put limits on her powers, such as the times when she has a sort of sensory overload (Which I can very much relate to!). While I do wonder how she was able to see the beavers building their dam – and thus blocking the river water from getting to the lake – all the way from the ThunderClan camp, I shared her enthusiasm when she set off to find them with the patrol of cats from all of the four Clans. I also felt her conflicted emotions at having such a great power yet being forced to keep it a secret. While I don't have too much to form a solid impression of her, this is the first book to feature her (aside from her birth toward the end of "Sunrise"), and I see some great potential in her as a character and as a warrior!<br /><br />Lionblaze – While I really liked Lionblaze in the "Power of Three" arc, it wasn't really until "Sunrise" that he became one of the most compelling characters in the series to me. That became all the more true in this book! Lionblaze has clearly grown and matured in pretty much every way from the time he was his new apprentice's age. For lack of a better way to put it, he feels not necessarily jaded but certainly more experienced. Whereas before he was the cocky young apprentice who was so eager to fight for his Clan that he was willing to learn from Tigerstar, he's since broken free of the latter's influence and is the valiant warrior he was always destined to be. He may not actually be Brambleclaw's son, but he certainly has a lot of his adoptive father's traits while remaining his own character. He's very passionate but will only charge into battle as a last resort. Like Brambleclaw, he's a natural leader even if he is unsure of himself at times. Not to mention, Dovepaw couldn't have a better mentor. I just loved their relationship, and how he wants to look out for her while also training her to become a warrior after his own heart. Plus, they're two of the three cats in the prophecy, so they have the shared dilemma and therefore the mutual understanding of having these great powers yet being forced to hide them. I also liked his relationship with his brother and therefore someone to share his grief over Hollyleaf's (supposed) death with. It felt like the brotherhood Brambleclaw and Hawkfrost could've had if Hawkfrost hadn't been seduced by the hunger for power he inherited from their father. Speaking of which, I am so glad that Lionblaze finally told Jayfeather about his dream sessions with Tigerstar!<br /><br />Jayfeather – I found Jayfeather just as compelling as his brother, though in his own interesting way. He's clearly the more distraught of the two of them over the loss of their sister. Not that Lionblaze doesn't feel terrible, but Jayfeather felt quite a bit more devastated, as evidenced by the fact that he blames himself for Hollyleaf's disappearance. That said, he's also the only one of the three cats in the prophecy who is attracted to the idea of holding the power of the stars in his paws. Not that I think he's drawn to power in the same way Tigerstar and Hawkfrost are, but he does kinda walk that shaky line. He's at best curious and at worst eager to be more powerful than StarClan. That said, while he's not the most touchy-feeling kind of medicine cat, he clearly does care about others. He cares about Lionblaze and Dovepaw not just because they're part of the prophecy but because they're his family, however much he denies that that's the case. It's no accident that he experiences Leafpool's memory of taking the strengthening herbs to Brambleclaw and Squirrelflight before they went on the quest to find Midnight. Speaking of which, even if he's still kind of mad at Leafpool, he misses having her and her medicine cat experience to help him do his duties, especially when he fails to prevent Firestar from losing a life. He goes out of his way to search for Poppyfrost and does his best to defend her from Breezepelt. Not to mention, he's capable of being just as passionate as Lionblaze, though, again, in his own way. I really felt bad for him when he finds out that Rock knew he was Leafpool's son. But then it truly floored me when he not only once again feels betrayed by someone he admired and looked up to, but also smashes the stick! That said, I can't wait to see what he learns about the coming battle between StarClan and the Dark Forest!<br /><br />The Patrol – I loved this callback to the journey the chosen cats took at the beginning of the "New Prophecy" arc! We got Toadfoot and Tigerheart from ShadowClan, Whitetail and Sedgewhisker from WindClan, and Petalfur and Rippletail from RiverClan. Toadfoot was a real pain in the tail at first, but fortunately he's not that big of a jerk. Even if he claims not to remember much of the Great Journey, he clearly at least somewhat remembers the sense of comradery. Tigerheart was probably my favorite! I thought his interactions with Dovepaw especially were adorable. He has this sense of chivalry about him and he clearly likes Dovepaw even though she's from a different Clan. And if his grandfather Tigerstar truly is training him, I can only say that I hope he turns away from him soon, 'cause I think he could really be a great example for future ShadowClan warriors to follow. Whitetail was clearly the most experienced warrior from any of the Clans, and I liked her leadership skills a lot. I was alarmed when Sedgewhisker got her foreleg wrenched, but I thought it was so cool that she went on and endured like it never even happened. I liked Rippletail a lot, and his loss was just a great blow to not only RiverClan but the patrol as well. Petalfur though was just fantastic. She doesn't so much get over Rippletail's death as she finds a new source of inspiration and determination to keep going in spite of it. All these cats played a really important part in the patrol, and they were fun to read about as they went on their adventure to dismantle the beavers' dam!<br /><br />Various Other Characters – I think it's so unfortunate that Squirrelflight and Leafpool are still reeling in the after effects of their lies having been revealed. I still like Brambleclaw but I hope he and Squirrelflight do eventually get back together. Besides, he's kept huge and old secrets from her as well! And while I do believe Leafpool made the right decision in resigning from being a medicine cat, I wish she could've at least been Jayfeather's assistant when it came to the herbs and remedies part of the occupation. Firestar as well feels as though he's getting on in his years. Not so much that he can't lead his Clan, but I can tell he's down to at least his last two lives. That said, I know he'll always be a great leader of ThunderClan to the bitter end. Speaking of which though, it was heartbreaking to see not only RiverClan but especially their leader Leopardstar suffering from the drought. Leopardstar has always been a great, strong, and fair leader, and to see her mentally and physically fading away was just heartbreaking. And speaking of that, I didn't think I'd get so wrapped up in the drama going on between Berrynose and Poppyfrost, but I did! As annoying as Berrynose can be, he does fiercely care about his loved ones, and it was so sad to read about Poppyfrost believing otherwise. Both cats deeply miss her sister Honeyfern, and I felt it. I was really glad though that Honeyfern told Jayfeather to tell her sister that she loves and misses both her and Berrynose, and that she'll watch over and love their kits. As for Breezepelt… Wow did he just descend to new levels of low, even for him! The worst of course is that he had the gall to attack Jayfeather, who's not just his half-brother but a medicine cat! I wanted to claw his muzzle and I hope some cat does that eventually! And last but not least, I liked Ivypaw's character even though she wasn't featured too much here. I thought it was a great idea to make Cinderheart her mentor, and I'm hoping she and Lionblaze get together! I'm already seeing the signs!<br /><br />Overall: This was a fantastic start to the "Omen of the Stars" arc! I can't wait to read more about Dovepaw's journey to becoming a warrior, and about how she, Lionblaze, and Jayfeather get used to being the Three. They're definitely going to need to that fast now that the countdown to the final confrontation between StarClan and the Dark Forest has started!</span>
  <a data-text-id="16550291150033767574" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1843666178" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1843666178" />
    <a title="Lexie Oberg" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/60072663-lexie-oberg"><img alt="Lexie Oberg" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475078406p2/60072663.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1843666178?book_show_action=true">Dec 19, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lexie Oberg" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lexie Oberg" href="/user/show/60072663-lexie-oberg">Lexie Oberg</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1843666178" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3193153654442612921">After the sharp-eyed jay and the roaring lion, peace will come…<br/>I loved reading Omen of the Stars, The Fourth Apprentice by Erin Hunter, a well-written and detailed fiction book. This book is part of a series within several series. If you haven’t read any of the books, here’s a brief overview of the base of each and every book. There are four warrior cat clans: ThunderClan, RiverClan, WindClan, and ShadowClan. In each clan, there is a clan leader, who leads with his/her appointed deputy, as well </span>
  <span id="freeText3193153654442612921" style="display:none">After the sharp-eyed jay and the roaring lion, peace will come…<br />I loved reading Omen of the Stars, The Fourth Apprentice by Erin Hunter, a well-written and detailed fiction book. This book is part of a series within several series. If you haven’t read any of the books, here’s a brief overview of the base of each and every book. There are four warrior cat clans: ThunderClan, RiverClan, WindClan, and ShadowClan. In each clan, there is a clan leader, who leads with his/her appointed deputy, as well as warriors, apprentices, elders, queens, and a medicine cat. The deputy commands all the cats in the clan and sends them on patrols. The leader chooses who goes to gatherings on the night of the full moon’s truce between the clans. A fight on the night of the truce would anger StarClan. The warriors hunt and patrol borders between the clans, as well as fight and go to gatherings. The medicine cat heals the cats in the clan. They journey to moonpool every time a half moon shows to share dreams with StarClan, their warrior ancestors who have died. They then return to their own clans. Queens are cats who have kits, and they stay in the nursery until their kits are six moons old. This is when the kits become apprentices and get assigned a mentor, while their mother returns to the warrior den and duties. The apprentices do things like change bedding, check for ticks on the elders, help out the warriors, and learn from their mentors. <br /><br />The content in this book continues from a previous series: Warriors, Power of Three.<br /><br />In Omen of the Stars, The Fourth Apprentice, the first two cats in the oldest prophecy find the third cat. This prophecy was created in Firestar’s Quest. “There will be three, kin of your kin, that will hold the power of the stars in their paws.” It was given to Firestar, ThunderClan’s noble leader, long ago. The prophecy was created by Cloudstar, the last leader of the original SkyClan (SkyClan was one of the ancient clans, but they were driven out of their territory by twolegs and forced into exile when the other clans wouldn’t share their territory. Firestar rebuilt the clan, and in return, Skywatcher gave this prophecy to him before he died). Each cat has a special power. The blind medicine cat, named Jayfeather, can see and feel other cats’ thoughts and feelings and gets signs and omens from StarClan. The golden warrior, named Lionblaze, cannot be defeated in battle, and the courageous apprentice, Dovepaw, can see and hear things that are very far away. Dovepaw senses a threat several miles upstream that is cutting off the water supply to the lake the warrior clans live around. The prophesied cats get two warriors from each clan to end the threat(Jayfeather stays back to care for the clan). How many warriors will die on this suicide mission? A secret revealed uncovers a threatening black cloud hovering over the clans as StarClan falls and the Dark Forest rises. <br />“ ‘It’s coming,’ Jayfeather whispered. ‘A battle between StarClan and the Dark Forest, and every warrior will be called upon to fight.’ ” <br />“ ‘They’re breaking through,” Lionblaze growled. “And when the battle comes, it will be for real.’ ”(final page)<br />This was, by far, my favorite book in the Omen of the Stars collection. It leads smoothly into the next books in the series and has many amazing details. When I read it, I feel like I’m there with the warrior clans. The books are all in the view of ThunderClan Cats, so you live the life of the cat whose point of view it is. I would definitely recommend this book for any reader who is looking for a fictional survival type of book, or if you are a cat lover like me. If you liked reading this, and even if you didn’t, I’d definitely recommend reading all of the books in all of the series. The collection that leads into the one this book is part of is called Warriors, Power of Three, and the book might make slightly more sense if you read at least the last book of Power of Three. I have read them all, and they are very hard to put down once you begin reading them. There are around 400-450 pages, depending on if you read it in paperback, on a phone, or on a computer. Published by Harpercollins Publishers.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3193153654442612921" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2224202369" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2224202369" />
    <a title="Lydia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/61228485-lydia"><img alt="Lydia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1565598651p2/61228485.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2224202369?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lydia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lydia" href="/user/show/61228485-lydia">Lydia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2224202369" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11646993183597827400">***NON-SPOILER PART OF REVIEW***<br/>About six moons after the last book Ivykit and Dovekit are to be apprenticed. It is still unknown which one is going to be the third cat of the prophecy. At this time a terrible drought is occurring where something is blocking the river that flows into the lake. The clans are hungry and hot, they are irritable, and no one knows why there is a drought. Dovepaw gets apprenticed to Lionblaze, while Ivypaw's mentor is Cinderheart. Cinderheart's sister, Poppyfrost is p</span>
  <span id="freeText11646993183597827400" style="display:none">***NON-SPOILER PART OF REVIEW***<br />About six moons after the last book Ivykit and Dovekit are to be apprenticed. It is still unknown which one is going to be the third cat of the prophecy. At this time a terrible drought is occurring where something is blocking the river that flows into the lake. The clans are hungry and hot, they are irritable, and no one knows why there is a drought. Dovepaw gets apprenticed to Lionblaze, while Ivypaw's mentor is Cinderheart. Cinderheart's sister, Poppyfrost is pregnant with Berrynose's kits by the way. There are patrols to collect water from the shrunken lake, and RiverClan is not happy that they are using the lake because they are starving because of a shortage of fish.<br /><br />***SPOILER PART OF REVIEW***<br />So, Breezepelt is furious at Leafpool, (who is now a warrior as a punishment) Lionblaze, and Jayfeather. Brambleclaw, Jayfeather and Lionblaze are still mad at Leafpool and Squirrelflight for lying, and Brambleclaw is no longer her mate. One day Dovepaw comments that there are brown animals who are building something that blocks the water. She says she has heard and seen them. She is confused why all of her clanmates are not believing her until Lionblaze tells her about the prophecy and how she has the power of extreme senses (don't know exactly how to explain it). She is upset at first, not wanting her sister to be left out. I think later Lionblaze tells Firstar that she had a dream from StarClan but I'm not sure. At the next gathering Firestar says that the each clan needs to send two cat to find out what is happening. From ThunderClan Lionblaze and Dovepaw are chosen. Sedgewhisker and Whitetail from WindClan. Blackstar sends Tigerheart and Toadstep. Leopardstar begrudgingly let's some of her weaker warriors go, Rippletail and Petalfur. Jayfeather meets Breezepelt at the lake when he is with some other ThunderClan warriors. Breezepelt makes it obvious he hates his half-brother by insulting his family. After a while of traveling the patrol finally gets to the source of their problem. Before they get there they meet three kittypets, Snowball, Jigsaw, and Seville. Back in ThunderClan the new queen, Poppyfrost is troubled with her relationship with Berrynose thinking he does not love her but Honeyfern, his former mate instead. She meets Jayfeather in her dream where she travels to the Moon Pool. Later she leaves the camp without telling anyone to try totalk to her sister at the moon pool. On the quest the cats all bond and become friends. They meet a loner named Woody who tells them the animals are beavers. The Clan cats try to attack the beavers and dislodge the dam but are unsuccessful. In the process Rippletail dies, which almost made me tear up. Jayfeather thinks that Poppyfrost is going to the moon pool and goes to find her. He scents that Breezepelt is following Poppyfrost. He catches up to Poppyfrost, but then Breezepelt attacks them. Trying to kill Jayfeather with the help of a mysterious to who is later revealed to be Brokenstar. With the help of Honeyfern's spirit Jayfeather drives away Brokenstar and Breezepelt. Yellowfang tells Jayfeather that a war between StarClan and The Place of no Stars is coming. The patrol forms a plan and with the help of the kittypets they met, they break the dam and defeat the beavers. They return as a group of seven instead of eight. Jayfeather learns Rock knew about his parents the whole time and breaks his stick in anger. Lionblaze tells Jayfeather how he had trained with Tigerstar.<br />*PERSONAL THOUGHTS*<br />I loved this. Power of Three kinda sucked, but this was wonderful. The story was quick and fun, the characters seemed less annoying. Great story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11646993183597827400" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_829536176" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/829536176" />
    <a title="Joyce" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21739770-joyce"><img alt="Joyce" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1393643025p2/21739770.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/829536176?book_show_action=true">Jan 20, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joyce" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joyce" href="/user/show/21739770-joyce">Joyce</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer829536176" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14765395427401951891">The start of another series!!! What I always disliked about new series was that most of the time the old, familiar characters had to be cast aside to make room for the new heroes. I'm so glad that for series, Jayfeather and Lionblaze stay in the spotlight. Their prophecy isn't fulfilled yet, but Dovepaw completes it! YAY!!! I LOVE Lionblaze and Jayfeather, and even though it's only been one book, I already love Dovepaw just as much. She is the last special cat, who has the power to know about th</span>
  <span id="freeText14765395427401951891" style="display:none">The start of another series!!! What I always disliked about new series was that most of the time the old, familiar characters had to be cast aside to make room for the new heroes. I'm so glad that for series, Jayfeather and Lionblaze stay in the spotlight. Their prophecy isn't fulfilled yet, but Dovepaw completes it! YAY!!! I LOVE Lionblaze and Jayfeather, and even though it's only been one book, I already love Dovepaw just as much. She is the last special cat, who has the power to know about things far away. It's nice how her power's pretty unique. Dovepaw is a great apprentice who has awesome skills, and I like how she's smart and strong, but also has the insecurities anyone would. I was so happy when Lionblaze became her mentor, and also when Cinderheart became Ivypaw's. They deserve it. I really miss Hollyleaf, and that's one of the reasons why this book seems different from Power of Three. And it was sad that Brambleclaw didn't like Squirrelflight anymore. Will he ever forgive her?! It's all Leafpool's fault! But anyway... This series is kind of like an add-on from the last, since that story was never really finished. Power of Three was like a prologue for this arc. The plot of The Fourth Apprentice was really interesting - Dovepaw, Lionblaze, and two cats from each Clan go upstream to locate the beavers that have dried up the lake, which caused a drought for all the Clans. I liked reading about the Clans working together again, and even uniting with kittypets and a loner in their plan. It was so great the Tigerheart (a warrior now!!) comes back into the story, as one of the warriors chosen to go on the journey. He and his littermates were always my favorites. In this book he seems to have a kind of crush on Dovepaw, and that made him all the more funny. While the cats were on their mission, Jayfeather deals with problems and discoveries around the lake. Breezepelt, who's being trained by Tigerstar, almost kills Poppyfrost and Jayfeather. And later on Jayfeather gets really mad at Rock, causing him to ACTUALLY SNAP HIS PRECIOUS STICK IN HALF, ON PURPOSE. I couldn't BELIEVE that, and I really wonder what happens next with the ancient cats. The book ends a little cliffhanger-y, with Jayfeather and Lionblaze knowing that StarClan and the Dark Forest will fight soon. How exactly can that happen?<br />This new series already feels distinct from the others, and AWESOME!!!!!!! I NEED TO GET THE NEXT BOOK! It seems like it's still the weekend, since I had 3 days off from school. But the good news for me is that as far away as Saturday may seem, it is actually only 3 more days from now. I'm CAN'T WAIT to read Fading Echoes!!! Everything is heating up now! The Dark Forest is rising!!! :D :D :D</span>
  <a data-text-id="14765395427401951891" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer18154200319194953130">After three four years of hiatus...I finally decided to continue reading Warriors! dun dun dun<br/>Truth be told, it's all thanks to <i>Watership Down</i>. I finished reading it last week and I couldn't get over how beautiful it was *here a single tear drops*. That eventually led me to think about Warriors since it was also a book about animals living like tribesmen of some sort. I wondered how my dear Brambleclaw was doing after he had his heart ripped apart in the last book I read (Sunrise). <br/>Let me just s</span>
  <span id="freeText18154200319194953130" style="display:none">After three four years of hiatus...I finally decided to continue reading Warriors! dun dun dun<br />Truth be told, it's all thanks to <i>Watership Down</i>. I finished reading it last week and I couldn't get over how beautiful it was *here a single tear drops*. That eventually led me to think about Warriors since it was also a book about animals living like tribesmen of some sort. I wondered how my dear Brambleclaw was doing after he had his heart ripped apart in the last book I read (Sunrise). <br />Let me just say it outright, I rather disliked the series from Starlight onwards. However I then did some research about the Omen of the Stars series. I read some spoilers and frankly that was the first time spoilers had a pleasant effect on me. It gave me goosebumps; my interest in the Warriors was renewed! I also found out that the latest series is about the <i>prequel</i> of the original series. So if I finish the Omen of the Stars series the whole matter would be over instead of leaving it hanging. My 10 year old inner self screamed out, "Yes, yes! Finally the Warriors series is <i>done</i>!!" With that logic, I decided to finish what I had started nearly 8 years ago. Thus I set off to the bookstore...<br /><br />Hehe, thank you for reading through that sad prologue. I'll get to my review now. <br />Well, there were some cheesey parts, just as I had expected. Nontheless, I still couldn't put the book down. Dovepaw was lovable one minute and the next I could have sworn I've read about characters like her hundreds of times already. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I also thought it odd how they didn't formally part with the kittypets and Woody. Then there's Breezepelt trying to kill an innocent pregnant cat?? what. i thought he was just a jerk not a psycho <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />All-in-all the book was well-flowing and an easy read, as with previous books. Sometimes it feels a bit rushed, or maybe that's due to my trying to finish it in one sitting. And, yes, I do have problems with the sometime-cheesiness. I highly recommend reading the previous series' before plunging into this one to prevent any confusion.<br /><br />Off to the bookstore again then sigghh</span>

    <a title="Pen High Library" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/63416889-pen-high-library"><img alt="Pen High Library" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1498153219p2/63416889.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2327732476?book_show_action=true">Mar 14, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pen High Library" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pen High Library" href="/user/show/63416889-pen-high-library">Pen High Library</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/63416889-pen-high-library?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2327732476" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5064591367346760400">“It has been foretold that Jayfeather and Lionblaze will hold the power of the stars in their paws.” This was what hooked me into the story because it made me wonder, what kind of powers do they have? How do they use them? And who is Jayfeather and Lionblaze? As the story goes on you discover that there are four clans around the lake that are gifted with powers passed down from their ancestors, there is tension and conflict between the clans because of the drought, instead of a lake with fish in</span>
  <span id="freeText5064591367346760400" style="display:none">“It has been foretold that Jayfeather and Lionblaze will hold the power of the stars in their paws.” This was what hooked me into the story because it made me wonder, what kind of powers do they have? How do they use them? And who is Jayfeather and Lionblaze? As the story goes on you discover that there are four clans around the lake that are gifted with powers passed down from their ancestors, there is tension and conflict between the clans because of the drought, instead of a lake with fish in it, it has become a giant mud puddle. <br /><br />The author’s writing style consists of narrative story telling along with some dialog which I enjoy a lot because its a more descriptive style of writing and it really immerses you, here is an example. “Long shadows stretched across the clearing as he padded to the pitifully small fresh kill pile, and the sky above the trees was streaked with scarlet. The scorching heat of the sun high and faded but the air was still heavy and stale.” Pg 54 <br /><br /> One of my favourite parts from the book was when one of the medicine cats had so much knowledge of the area that she was able to gather some herbs and heal a wounded warrior cat, I thought this part was cool because it shows just how magical these cats are. I would highly recommend this book to people that enjoy fantasy stories filled with action and suspense that will leave you anxious to keep reading.<br /></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('8Tz7Js4Mu8nDyK19zTDdoangaa16sicTKB2/H5G/VRjSy6L2psNKCoz75SJjvPzd/89QhSo8JlcClh9AcVsEZA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('CfdFzxiuJfoSVzTtdAtcN2rubL7GB5jLpZRYdmp1wWcqABwfcGHUOV1kfLLah31LPMFVlpaJmY+PH/gpipGQGw==')})
  }

  <span id="freeText8215579203097067813" style="display:none">Erin Hunter is the pseudonym of five people: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/132369.Kate_Cary" title="Kate Cary" rel="nofollow noopener">Kate Cary</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/220345.Cherith_Baldry" title="Cherith Baldry" rel="nofollow noopener">Cherith Baldry</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/374504.Tui_T__Sutherland" title="Tui T. Sutherland" rel="nofollow noopener">Tui T. Sutherland</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2742182.Gillian_Philip" title="Gillian Philip" rel="nofollow noopener">Gillian Philip</a>, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/769868.Inbali_Iserles" title="Inbali Iserles" rel="nofollow noopener">Inbali Iserles</a>, as well as editor <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/645010.Victoria_Holmes" title="Victoria Holmes" rel="nofollow noopener">Victoria Holmes</a>. Together, they write the Warriors series as well as the Seekers and Survivors series. Erin Hunter is working on a new series now called Bravelands. <br /><br />Erin Hunter is inspired by a love of cats and a fascination with the ferocity of the natural world. As well as having a great respect for nature in all its forms, Erin enjoys creating rich mythical explanations for animal behavior, shaped by her interest in astronomy and standing stones.</span>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/6432575-the-fourth-apprentice-warriors-omen-of-the-stars-1">Quotes from The Fourth Appren...</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Welcome to our camp!" Blackstar called, beckoning them with his tail. "Rest here and take your pick of the fresh-kill pile."<br /><br />"Who are you and what have you done with Blackstar?" Lionblaze muttered.&rdquo;</span>
